Fast, fresh, and good prices. Had a great Sour Beer on tap from a local brewery!  Nice tap beer selection; but also carry bottles, wine & Sake. The alcohol prices are a bit high. Staff is friendly and want to help with any questions you may have. No challenges having what you want in your bowl to eat. I've been twice now and will go back again when I'm in a hurry to eat fresh. They also have vegan and gluten free. There's enough seating so you don't feel crowded and can enjoy conversation with whomever you're with.< /review>

Well, just got done reading Rae Sto‚Äôs one-star comment - and man, some people really do buy into this victim trend. Sorry lady, you‚Äôre not royalty, the world is not out to get you, they DO have smaller selections to choose from and you can always share a plate or eat a little at a time and use a fridge. Weird that you felt you needed to bring race into it.

That‚Äôs a vicious way to talk about a small business trying to get a good start, especially when the owner is working to reach out to you in good faith (and you DID give Taco Bell a 4-star review, so... come on.)

That being said: Lemonshark is a sweet little poke restaurant. This place is nice and open, clean, aesthetically pleasing, has a great vibe, and provides consistently solid food. The fish tastes fresh, the veggie selection is vibrant and there‚Äôs a much larger selection than a lot of their competition. Good beers on tap and I like their cherry soda (w/ tarragon!). Great place for dates or to come after a workout. The food sits easy on my stomach and they have a ton of probiotic/anti-inflammatory goods to sprinkle on top (seaweed salad, ginger, etc.). Keep it rocking guys, I love seeing stuff like this pop up in the valley, it‚Äôs much needed. You‚Äôve got my support and that of my fam.<//review>

I ran into so many problems with this location. Some of them are due to booking through Priceline, but Enterprise should be taking it upon themselves to make sure the information given through Priceline is accurate. (Also, the Enterprise mobile app would not work so booking directly was not an option for us).

First, when booking, we were given the full range of pickup times. But when we actually went to go pick up at 1pm as we had scheduled, I saw that the place actually closed at 1 that day. We called them on our drive over to make sure we would still be able to pick it up at that time and that they wouldn't close without giving us our car. They seemed surprised and a little hesitant. It was a seriously good thing we even saw the hours by chance and that we decided to call... what would have happened otherwise?

Secondly, we were told when booking through Priceline that our car would have unlimited mileage. This is the main reason why we decided we could afford to get this particular car (it was a luxury car but with the unlimited mileage would only work out to about $50 extra for the whole time so we figured it was worth it.) However, when we get there, we learn it's an extra $20 a day for unlimited miles with a luxury car. Thankfully the woman helping us (who was very nice) said she could get us $10/day since that wasn't our fault. Somewhat better, but still frustrating.

The car was only filled to 7/8 of a tank when we picked it up, so she said we only had to refill it to 7/8 when returning it. Not that big of a deal, but it is very hard to estimate filling up the car to 7/8 as opposed to full... we tried but ended up overfilling, so that was a few bucks lost.

I also didn't know this, but Enterprise doesn't go through credit cards for insurance at all like many rental agencies do. I tried looking this information up before renting and couldn't find it anywhere, but I guess it's not on them that I didn't know this. Anyway, so then to insure the car against damage I had to pay an extra $31 a day (again, another discrepancy between Priceline and Enterprise--Priceline's website said this would be $13/day).

We were also misinformed by the woman who helped us that our car would take 87 gas. Not the case. It only took 91.

Additionally, the car's tires kept losing pressure, reaching dangerously low levels one day after another, and we had to refill them twice on our own dime. That was really inconvenient and confusing as to what was causing it.

Anyway, long story short, we thought we were getting a really good deal at first and then the little costs just kept adding up. Though the employees were friendly and few of these problems were their fault, I won't go through Enterprise again. If you must book with them, definitely do everything in your power to book directly with them and not through a third party. Ask tons of detailed questions before you book.<//Text>

<review>Take note that the low star ratings are limited in number and they are not a reliable reflection of Enterprise's overall performance.  My agency has a contract with Enterprise, so I am there on a frequent basis, and I give my rating based on more than an isolated encounter.  The staff are always courteous and informative, and I know their drivers on a first name basis.  The foregoing said, every once in a while I see customers who fail to listen closely to what the staff says, trying to place blame for their own inattention on the staff.  In response to one of the one star posts I read, yes, insurance via Enterprise is optional, and yes, Enterprise will offer it to each customer with an advisement that it is their choice to purchase it ... when it is offered, if you decide for forego a call to your insurance carrier to get their input, don't blame someone else.  Also, if you don't drive a high end car but are in an accident with your car in the shop and end up making a decision to rent a higher end model, I doubt the staff at Enterprise did any arm twisting to rent a car that would put the customer out of pocket ... I've always heard each representative ask the make a model of the car in the shop so they can put the customer into a comparable vehicle.   If you need a rental vehicle, I would always suggest that you make Enterprise your first choice.</review><pics>None< /pics><response>None< /response><Gmap_id>0x80e82522734e4bb3:0x3d0d503e23f88b5< /Gmap_id></record>

<time>1498835183612<//time>< Rating>
4<//Rating>
< text>
I have used Enterprise Rent-A-Car at this location a lot, like 50+ days of rental in 2 years.  Originally,  I gave them a solid 5-star rating, but after my most recent rentals, I decided that, to be honest, I can no longer do that.

Service has always been very good in the sense that they picked me up within a reasonable amount of time, drove me back promptly,  personnel was overall very polite and helpful, and their prices have been overall competitive.
However,  as this location prides itself to be the busiest Enterprise location outside of airports, in my opinion they are starting to suffer from their own success. In fact, the last 3 rentals, by the time I got there to pick up my car (and it was not on late afternoon on Fridays before the w/e begins) the choice of cars available was truly weak: basically just one car and we were staring at an empty lot so that even upgrading to a higher class was not an option. They probably decided to reduce their inventory, and that is fine, but this will force me to reconsider my loyalty to them. I am also a little annoyed that their cars are almost never ready with a full tank of gas. In some occasions cars were not very clean either.  Sure, if I am lucky and I get a very new one, chances are it is in pristine conditions, but if the car has 20-30k it come with stained seats (in particular the back seats where kids often seat), smudges everywhere on the console, etc.  That is not cool.
I also could appreciate cleaner side mirrors. Too often they have been full of dead water stains which, in the California' sun, can make it hard to monitor traffic on the road.  These are minor things that are easy to fix and will show a tad more attention to details.  Finally, there is a huge personnel rotation. After one year, there is not a single  person with whom I had developed some familiarity.  Their exotic car rentals is a nice addition, but they keep just a minimal inventory and so every car has to be booked in advance. It is not likely that, say, one w/e you get there, see a nice exotic cars (and I am not even talking the supercars for $1000+/day, but the more common ones like Porsches, Audis, BMWs, etc.)  and decide to treat yourself to one of those. Nope, most often those are for clients who reserved them and are about to pick them up. For many months they were under renovation and as a customer I was sold that they were improving to increase their offerings, including exotics, but that did not really happen, not the way I would have hoped at least. So, to conclude, personnel is still 5-star, but their product is not. Hence my 4-star rating.<//text>

< Review>
Evening Rose Cafe is a quaint little restaurant tucked off of the highway in Nice, CA. They serve delicious breakfast with good-sized portions. They also have sandwiches and  entrees and if you're hungry for a little something more they accommodate that too. The only downside is that they're only open till 2 p.m. but I think that's also part of what makes them special. It's never super crowded. They always have a good amount of customers, most of whom are regulars, but it's not so noisy and overcrowded that it's uncomfortable. The food is really really good and they can accommodate special orders. Not organic foods but if you want something left out that you don't like or if you want a special omelette they will make it for you if they can. The decor is nothing special it's just very small and very quaint and very comfortable. it's never too cold in there. It's never too warm in there. It's just a comfortable tiny little place that I've referred to as a hole in the wall, even though it's too quaint to be called a hole in the wall, that has really good food and I suggest giving it a try. I think you'll be pleasantly surprised. One more thing you can call or walk in for to-go order requests.</Review>

I brought the bubbly water back to Devon without touching it, saying, you know, that's kind of a lot; I'll just have tap. I'm cool about it, he's cool about it, but it was an ordeal getting my card credited. Which it never was. I was charged $37, and then $34 again.

She asked, "No?"
